       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_Forbes_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_Forbes-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>47</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_USNWR_NU_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_USNWR_NU-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>30</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_Wamo_NU_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_Wamo_NU-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>4</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th colspan="2" style="background-color: lavender; text-align: center">Global</th> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">ARWU</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_ARWU_W_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_ARWU_W-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>41</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>57</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_THES_W_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_THES_W-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>42</td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>In 2011, the <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked UNC Chapel Hill 5th among the nation's top public colleges and universities.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university was named a <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> by Richard Moll in his 1985 book <i>The Public Ivies: A Guide to America's Best Public Undergraduate Colleges and Universities</i>, and in later guides by Howard and Matthew Greene.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of UNC's professional schools have achieved high rankings in publications such as <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes_Magazine" title="Forbes Magazine" class="mw-redirect">Forbes Magazine</a></i>, as well as annual <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> surveys.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> ranked UNC business school's MBA program as the 20th best in the United States. In the 2011 edition, <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> ranked the UNC <a href="/wiki/Gillings_School_of_Global_Public_Health" title="Gillings School of Global Public Health" class="mw-redirect">Gillings School of Global Public Health</a> as the top <i>public</i> school of public health in the United States, and the second ranked school of public health in the nation (behind the top ranked school, Johns Hopkins and ahead of the third ranked school, Harvard).<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bare_url_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bare_url-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/UNC_Eshelman_School_of_Pharmacy" title="UNC Eshelman School of Pharmacy">UNC Eshelman School of Pharmacy</a> was ranked second among pharmacy schools in the United States in 2012 by the U.S. News &amp; World Report.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2005, <i>Business Week</i> ranked UNC business school's Executive MBA program as the 5th best in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Other highly ranked schools include journalism and mass communication, law, library and information studies, medicine, dentistry, and city and regional planning.<sup id="cite_ref-bare_url_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bare_url-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Nationally, UNC is in the top ten public universities for research.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Internationally, the 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> ranked North Carolina 57th overall in the world, moving up 21 places from its position of 78th in the 2009 <a href="/wiki/THE-QS_World_University_Rankings" title="THE-QS World University Rankings" class="mw-redirect">THE-QS World University Rankings</a> (in 2010 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> and <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> parted ways to produce separate rankings).</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:North_Carolina_Collection.jpg" class="image"><img alt=" A room filled with many tables and chairs and bookshelves lining the walls." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/North_Carolina_Collection.jpg/220px-North_Carolina_Collection.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/North_Carolina_Collection.jpg/330px-North_Carolina_Collection.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/North_Carolina_Collection.jpg/440px-North_Carolina_Collection.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:North_Carolina_Collection.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The NCC is the largest collection of printed materials related to a single state.
        <sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UNC's undergraduate program is ranked 30th in the United States by the U.S. News &amp; World Report and is consistently ranked among the nation's top five public universities, just behind <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">UC Berkeley</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Kiplinger%27s_Personal_Finance" title="Kiplinger's Personal Finance">Kiplinger's Personal Finance</a></i> has also ranked UNC as the number one &quot;best value&quot; public college for in-state students.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Similarly, the university is first among public universities and ninth overall in &quot;Great Schools, Great Prices&quot;, on the basis of academic quality, net cost of attendance and average student debt.<sup id="cite_ref-US_News:_America.27s_Best_Colleges_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_News:_America.27s_Best_Colleges-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Along with one of the nation's most acclaimed undergraduate honors programs in a public institution, UNC also has the highest percentage of undergraduates studying abroad for any public institution.<sup id="cite_ref-compendium_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-compendium-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2012, however, widespread academic fraud was detected at the university, when an investigation found that many courses in the Afro-American Studies Department were entirely pro-forma, wherein students could get a passing grade for submitting &quot;term papers&quot; without attending any classes. Going back to as far as 1997, 216 classes were found to have potential or proven problems, and at least 454 student grades were changed without authorization. The investigation laid the fault for these irregularities entirely at the foot of two people: former Afro-American Studies Department chairman Julius Nyang'oro, and former administrator Deborah Crowder.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> No other members of the faculty, staff, or administration were found responsible for any misconduct. Nevertheless, questions continue to be raised about just how endemic these problems are at North Carolina.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scholarships">Scholarships</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Scholarships">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Morehead-Cain_Scholarship" title="Morehead-Cain Scholarship">Morehead-Cain Scholarship</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Robertson_Scholars_Program" title="Robertson Scholars Program">Robertson Scholars Program</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UNC_Graham_Memorial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large brick building with columns on the front and three doors." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/UNC_Graham_Memorial.jpg/220px-UNC_Graham_Memorial.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/UNC_Graham_Memorial.jpg/330px-UNC_Graham_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/UNC_Graham_Memorial.jpg/440px-UNC_Graham_Memorial.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UNC_Graham_Memorial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Graham Memorial is adjacent to 
        <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Street_(Chapel_Hill)" title="Franklin Street (Chapel Hill)">Franklin Street</a> and houses the Office for Undergraduate Research and the Honors Study Abroad program.
        <sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup>
        <sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>For decades UNC has offered an undergraduate merit scholarship known as the Morehead-Cain Scholarship. Recipients receive tuition, room and board, books, and funds for summer study for four years. Since the inception of the Morehead scholarship program, 29 alumni of the program have been named <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> North Carolina also boasts the Robertson Scholars Program, a scholarship granting recipients the opportunity to attend both UNC and neighboring Duke University.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, the university provides merit-based scholarships, including the Carolina, Colonel Robinson, and Pogue Scholars programs, which offer full scholarships for out-of-state students.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2003, Chancellor <a href="/wiki/James_Moeser" title="James Moeser">James Moeser</a> announced the Carolina Covenant, which provides a debt free education to low-income students who are academically qualified to attend the university. The program was the second in the nation (following <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton</a>) and the first of its kind at a public university. About 80 other universities have since followed suit.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>North Carolina is tied for the largest number of Rhodes Scholars among public universities (47 since 1902) with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, many students have won <a href="/wiki/Truman_Scholarship" title="Truman Scholarship" class="mw-redirect">Truman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barry_M._Goldwater_Scholarship" title="Barry M. Goldwater Scholarship">Goldwater</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Scholarship" title="Mitchell Scholarship">Mitchell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Churchill_Scholarship" title="Churchill Scholarship">Churchill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_Program" title="Fulbright Program">Fulbright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Scholarship" title="Marshall Scholarship">Marshall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morris_K._Udall_Foundation#Morris_K._Udall_Undergraduate_Scholarships" title="Morris K. Udall Foundation" class="mw-redirect">Udall</a>, and Mellon scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels" title="North Carolina Tar Heels">North Carolina Tar Heels</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The inside of a basketball dome with two teams on a court with a large logo in the shape of the state of North Carolina in the middle." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg/220px-Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg/330px-Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg/440px-Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Duke-Carolina_basketball_tip-off_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Tip-off of a basketball game against Duke at the 
        <a href="/wiki/Dean_Smith_Center" title="Dean Smith Center">Smith Center</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>North Carolina's athletic teams are known as the Tar Heels. They compete as a member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA) <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> level (Football Bowl Subdivision (FBS) sub-level for football), primarily competing in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> (ACC) for all sports since the 1953?54 season.<sup id="cite_ref-acc_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acc-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Men's sports include baseball, basketball, cross country, fencing, football, golf, lacrosse, soccer, swimming &amp; diving, tennis, track &amp; field and wrestling; while women's sports include basketball, cross country, fencing, field hockey, golf, gymnastics, lacrosse, rowing, soccer, softball, swimming and diving, tennis, track &amp; field and volleyball.</p> 
     <p>The NCAA refers to UNC as the &quot;University of North Carolina&quot; for athletics.<sup id="cite_ref-ncaaschools_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ncaaschools-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> As of Fall 2011, the university had won 40 NCAA team championships in six different sports, eighth all-time.<sup id="cite_ref-NCAA_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCAA-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> These include twenty one NCAA championships in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_women%27s_soccer" title="North Carolina Tar Heels women's soccer">women's soccer</a>, six in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_field_hockey" title="North Carolina Tar Heels field hockey">women's field hockey</a>, four in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_lacrosse" title="North Carolina Tar Heels men's lacrosse">men's lacrosse</a>, five in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball">men's basketball</a>, one in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_women%27s_basketball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels women's basketball">women's basketball</a>, and two in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_soccer" title="North Carolina Tar Heels men's soccer">men's soccer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> The Men's basketball team won its 5th NCAA basketball championship in 2009, the second for Coach Roy Williams since he took the job as head coach. Other recent successes include the 2011 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Soccer_Championship" title="NCAA Division I Men's Soccer Championship">College Cup</a> in men's soccer, and four consecutive <a href="/wiki/College_World_Series" title="College World Series">College World Series</a> appearances by the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_baseball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels baseball">baseball team</a> from 2006 to 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1994, the university's athletic programs won the <a href="/wiki/NACDA_Director%27s_Cup" title="NACDA Director's Cup" class="mw-redirect">Sears Directors Cup</a> &quot;all-sports national championship&quot; awarded for cumulative performance in NCAA competition.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> Consensus collegiate national athletes of the year from North Carolina include <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Dawson" title="Rachel Dawson">Rachel Dawson</a> in field hockey; <a href="/wiki/Phil_Ford_(basketball)" title="Phil Ford (basketball)">Phil Ford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Hansbrough" title="Tyler Hansbrough">Tyler Hansbrough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antawn_Jamison" title="Antawn Jamison">Antawn Jamison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vince_Carter" title="Vince Carter">Vince Carter</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Worthy" title="James Worthy">James Worthy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jordan" title="Michael Jordan">Michael Jordan</a> in men's basketball; and <a href="/wiki/Mia_Hamm" title="Mia Hamm">Mia Hamm</a> (twice), <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Higgins-Cirovski" title="Shannon Higgins-Cirovski">Shannon Higgins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kristine_Lilly" title="Kristine Lilly">Kristine Lilly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tisha_Venturini" title="Tisha Venturini">Tisha Venturini</a> in women's soccer.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot_and_nickname">Mascot and nickname</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Mascot and nickname">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Devil_and_Rameses.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A man dressed as a devil and a ram face each other." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f8/Blue_Devil_and_Rameses.jpg/220px-Blue_Devil_and_Rameses.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f8/Blue_Devil_and_Rameses.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f8/Blue_Devil_and_Rameses.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Devil_and_Rameses.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Rameses at the 1957 
        <a href="/wiki/Victory_Bell_(Carolina-Duke)" title="Victory Bell (Carolina-Duke)" class="mw-redirect">Victory Bell</a> football game
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university's teams are nicknamed the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Tar_Heel" title="Tar Heel">Tar Heels</a>,&quot; in reference to the state's eighteenth century prominence as a <a href="/wiki/Tar" title="Tar">tar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pitch_(resin)" title="Pitch (resin)">pitch</a> producer.<sup id="cite_ref-heel_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heel-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> The nickname's cultural relevance, however, has a complex history that includes anecdotal tales from both the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heel_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heel-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> The mascot is a live <a href="/wiki/Dorset_(sheep)" title="Dorset (sheep)">Dorset ram</a> named <a href="/wiki/Rameses_(mascot)" title="Rameses (mascot)">Rameses</a>, a tradition that dates back to 1924, when the team manager brought a ram to the annual game against <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Military_Institute" title="Virginia Military Institute">Virginia Military Institute</a>, inspired by the play of former football player Jack &quot;<a href="/wiki/Battering_ram" title="Battering ram">The Battering Ram</a>&quot; Merrit. The kicker rubbed his head for good luck before a game-winning field goal, and the ram stayed.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> There is also an <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphic" title="Anthropomorphic" class="mw-redirect">anthropomorphic</a> ram mascot who appears at games.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> The modern Rameses is depicted in a sailor's hat, a reference to a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> flight training program that was attached to the university during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Carolina-Duke_rivalry" title="Carolina-Duke rivalry" class="mw-redirect">Duke Rivalry</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Carolina-NC_State_rivalry" title="Carolina-NC State rivalry" class="mw-redirect">North Carolina State Rivalry</a>, and 
      <a href="/wiki/South%27s_Oldest_Rivalry" title="South's Oldest Rivalry">South's Oldest Rivalry</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/South%27s_Oldest_Rivalry_(UNC-Virginia)" title="South's Oldest Rivalry (UNC-Virginia)" class="mw-redirect">South's Oldest Rivalry</a> between North Carolina and its first opponent, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a>, was prominent throughout much of the twentieth century.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> September 2012 saw the 121st meeting in <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">football</a> between the two teams.</p> 
     <p>One of the fiercest rivalries is with Durham's <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke University</a>. Located only eight miles from each other, the schools regularly compete in both athletics and academics. The <a href="/wiki/Carolina-Duke_rivalry" title="Carolina-Duke rivalry" class="mw-redirect">Carolina-Duke rivalry</a> is most intense, however, in <a href="/wiki/College_basketball" title="College basketball">basketball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hbo_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hbo-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> With a combined nine national championships in men's basketball, both teams have been frequent contenders for the national championship for the past thirty years. The rivalry has been the focus of several books, including Will Blythe's <i>To Hate Like This Is to Be Happy Forever</i> and was the focus of the HBO documentary <i>Battle for Tobacco Road: Duke vs Carolina</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Carolina holds an intense in-state rivalry with fellow Tobacco Road school, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State_University" title="North Carolina State University">North Carolina State University</a>. While attention shifted to Duke following a decline in NC State's basketball program since the 1980s, the rivalry is still held as one of the most bitter in the state. Combined, the two schools hold seven NCAA Championships and 27 ACC Championships in basketball. Students from each school often exchange pranks before basketball and football games.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_Street_Celebration.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large gathering of people on a street with a bonfire in the right side of the image." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Franklin_Street_Celebration.jpg/220px-Franklin_Street_Celebration.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Franklin_Street_Celebration.jpg/330px-Franklin_Street_Celebration.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/Franklin_Street_Celebration.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_Street_Celebration.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Celebration on 
        <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Street_(Chapel_Hill)" title="Franklin Street (Chapel Hill)">Franklin Street</a> after victory over Duke
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rushing_Franklin">Rushing Franklin</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Rushing Franklin">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>While students previously held &quot;Beat <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke</a>&quot; parades on <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Street_(Chapel_Hill)" title="Franklin Street (Chapel Hill)">Franklin Street</a> before sporting events,<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> today students and sports fans have been known to spill out of bars and dormitories upon the victory of one of Carolina's sports <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels" title="North Carolina Tar Heels">teams</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-scene_from_franklin_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scene_from_franklin-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> In most cases, a Franklin Street &quot;bonfire&quot; celebration is due to a <a href="/wiki/Carolina-Duke_rivalry" title="Carolina-Duke rivalry" class="mw-redirect">victory</a> by the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball">men's basketball team</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bonfire_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bonfire-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fire_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fire-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> although other Franklin Street celebrations have stemmed from wins by the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_women%27s_basketball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels women's basketball">women's basketball team</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels" title="North Carolina Tar Heels">women's soccer team</a>. The first known student celebration on Franklin Street came after the <a href="/wiki/1956%E2%80%9357_North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1956?57 North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball team">1957 men's basketball team</a> capped their perfect season with a National Championship victory over the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Jayhawks" title="Kansas Jayhawks">Kansas Jayhawks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chapelhillnews1_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chapelhillnews1-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> From then on, students have flooded the street after important victories.<sup id="cite_ref-chapelhillnews1_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chapelhillnews1-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> After a <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" title="Final Four" class="mw-redirect">Final Four</a> victory in <a href="/wiki/1981_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="1981 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1981</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1981?82 North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball team">men's basketball team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/1982_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="1982 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1982 NCAA Championship</a>, Franklin Street was painted blue by the fans who had rushed the street.<sup id="cite_ref-chapelhillnews1_146-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chapelhillnews1-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> This event has led local vendors to stop selling Carolina blue paint as the Tar Heels near the national championship.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_colors">School colors</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: School colors">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Since the beginning of intercollegiate athletics at UNC in the late nineteenth century, the school's colors have been <a href="/wiki/Carolina_blue" title="Carolina blue">Carolina blue</a> also known as &quot;baby blue&quot; and white.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> The colors were chosen years before by the <a href="/wiki/Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies" title="Dialectic and Philanthropic Societies">Dialectic (blue) and Philanthropic (white) Societies</a>, the oldest student organization at the university. The school had required participation in one of the clubs, and traditionally the &quot;Di&quot;s were from the western part of North Carolina while the &quot;Phi&quot;s were from the eastern part of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-Carolina_Review.2C_vol._XIII.2C_no._6_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carolina_Review.2C_vol._XIII.2C_no._6-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Commencement_Ceremony_at_Kenan_Memorial_Stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A bunch of people standing with cap and gowns while two people stand on a grass field." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Commencement_Ceremony_at_Kenan_Memorial_Stadium.jpg/220px-Commencement_Ceremony_at_Kenan_Memorial_Stadium.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Commencement_Ceremony_at_Kenan_Memorial_Stadium.jpg/330px-Commencement_Ceremony_at_Kenan_Memorial_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/96/Commencement_Ceremony_at_Kenan_Memorial_Stadium.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Commencement_Ceremony_at_Kenan_Memorial_Stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 2007 commencement ceremony in 
        <a href="/wiki/Kenan_Memorial_Stadium" title="Kenan Memorial Stadium">Kenan Memorial Stadium</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Society members would wear a blue or white ribbon at university functions, and blue or white ribbons were attached to their diplomas at graduation.<sup id="cite_ref-Carolina_Review.2C_vol._XIII.2C_no._6_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carolina_Review.2C_vol._XIII.2C_no._6-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> On public occasions, both groups were equally represented, and eventually both colors were used by processional leaders to signify the unity of both groups as part of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> When football became a popular collegiate sport in the 1880s, the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_football" title="North Carolina Tar Heels football">UNC football</a> team adopted the light blue and white of the Di-Phi Societies as the school colors.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_songs">School songs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: School songs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Notable among a number of songs commonly played and sung at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, and athletic games are the university <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight songs</a> &quot;<a href="/wiki/I%27m_a_Tar_Heel_Born" title="I'm a Tar Heel Born" class="mw-redirect">I'm a Tar Heel Born</a>&quot; and &quot;<a href="/wiki/Here_Comes_Carolina" title="Here Comes Carolina" class="mw-redirect">Here Comes Carolina</a>&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-songs_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-songs-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> The fight songs are often played by the bell tower near the center of campus, as well as after major victories.<sup id="cite_ref-songs_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-songs-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> &quot;I?m a Tar Heel Born&quot; originated in the late 1920s as a tag to the school's alma mater, &quot;<a href="/wiki/Hark_The_Sound" title="Hark The Sound">Hark The Sound</a>&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-songs_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-songs-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> &quot;Hark the Sound&quot; was usually played at the end of games, but as of late it has been played at the beginning of games as well.</p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A collection of people sitting in a white room that has paintings on its walls." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies.jpg/220px-Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies.jpg/330px-Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies.jpg/440px-Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies" title="Dialectic and Philanthropic Societies">Dialectic and Philanthropic Societies</a> of UNC were founded in 1795 and have debates each week in the New West building.
        <sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizations_and_activities">Organizations and activities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Organizations and activities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Most student organizations at UNC are officially recognized and provided with assistance by the Carolina Union, an administrative unit of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> Funding is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Student_government" title="Student government" class="mw-redirect">student government</a> student activity fee, which is allocated at the discretion of the student congress.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The largest student fundraiser, the UNC Dance Marathon, involves thousands of students, faculty, and community members in raising funds for the <a href="/wiki/UNC_Health_Care" title="UNC Health Care">North Carolina Children's Hospital</a>. The organization conducts fundraising and volunteer activities throughout the year and, as of 2008, had donated $1.4&nbsp;million since its inception in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University is also noted for its <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://campus-y.unc.edu">Campus Y</a>, the social justice hub on campus that houses many service and internationally focused organizations. The Campus Y was founded in 1859, and is noted as a &quot;leader in on-campus discussion and dialogue and off-campus service and activism&quot;. The Campus Y was at the center of many progressive movements within the university, including the racial integration of the student body, the effort to improve wages and working conditions for University employees,and the establishment of the Sonja Haynes Stones Center for Black Culture and History. The Y is a collection of many UNC specific and outside organizations, such as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://carolinakickoff.unc.edu">Carolina Kickoff</a>, STAND, Nourish International, Carolina Microfinance Initiative, Homeless Outreach &amp; Poverty Eradication (HOPE), and Project Literacy.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:2008-07-11_UNC-CH_Forest_Theatre_(top_view).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A stone amphitheater in the wooden location." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/2008-07-11_UNC-CH_Forest_Theatre_%28top_view%29.jpg/220px-2008-07-11_UNC-CH_Forest_Theatre_%28top_view%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/2008-07-11_UNC-CH_Forest_Theatre_%28top_view%29.jpg/330px-2008-07-11_UNC-CH_Forest_Theatre_%28top_view%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/2008-07-11_UNC-CH_Forest_Theatre_%28top_view%29.jpg/440px-2008-07-11_UNC-CH_Forest_Theatre_%28top_view%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:2008-07-11_UNC-CH_Forest_Theatre_(top_view).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Forest Theatre was first used for outdoor drama in 1916 to celebrate the tercentenary of 
        <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">Shakespeare's</a> death.
        <sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The student run newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Tar_Heel" title="The Daily Tar Heel">The Daily Tar Heel</a></i> is ranked highly by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> and received the 2004?5 <a href="/wiki/National_Pacemaker_Awards" title="National Pacemaker Awards">National Pacemaker Award</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Collegiate_Press" title="Associated Collegiate Press">Associated Collegiate Press</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> Founded in 1977, <a href="/wiki/WXYC" title="WXYC">WXYC</a> 89.3 FM is UNC's student radio station that broadcasts 24&nbsp;hours a day, 365&nbsp;days a year. Programming is left up to student DJs. WXYC typically plays little heard music from a wide range of genres and eras. On November 7, 1994, WXYC became the first radio station in the world to broadcast its signal over the internet.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> A student-run television station, <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill_Student_Television" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill Student Television">STV</a>, airs on the campus cable and throughout the Chapel Hill <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner_Cable" title="Time Warner Cable">Time Warner Cable</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> Founded in 1948 as successor to the <i>Carolina Magazine</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> the <i>Carolina Quarterly</i>, edited by graduate students, has published the works of numerous authors, including <a href="/wiki/Wendell_Berry" title="Wendell Berry">Wendell Berry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Carver" title="Raymond Carver">Raymond Carver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_DeLillo" title="Don DeLillo">Don DeLillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annie_Dillard" title="Annie Dillard">Annie Dillard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joyce_Carol_Oates" title="Joyce Carol Oates">Joyce Carol Oates</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Edgar_Wideman" title="John Edgar Wideman">John Edgar Wideman</a>. Works appearing in the <i>Quarterly</i> have been anthologized in <i><a href="/wiki/Best_American_Short_Stories" title="Best American Short Stories" class="mw-redirect">Best American Short Stories</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/New_Stories_from_the_South" title="New Stories from the South">New Stories from the South</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> and have won the <a href="/wiki/Pushcart_Prize" title="Pushcart Prize">Pushcart</a> and <a href="/wiki/O._Henry_Prize" title="O. Henry Prize" class="mw-redirect">O. Henry Prizes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Residence Hall Association, the school's third-largest student-run organization, is dedicated to enhancing the experience of students living in residence halls. This includes putting on social, educational, and philanthropic programs for residents; recognizing outstanding residents and members; and helping residents develop into successful leaders. The organization is run by 8 student executive officers; 16 student governors that represent each residence hall community; and numerous community government members. RHA is the campus organization of <a href="/wiki/NACURH" title="NACURH" class="mw-redirect">NACURH</a>, the largest student organization in the world. In 2010 the organization won the national RHA Building Block Award, which is awarded to the school with the most improved RHA organization.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UNC_library_flash_mob_rave.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large gathering of people in a room." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/UNC_library_flash_mob_rave.jpg/220px-UNC_library_flash_mob_rave.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/UNC_library_flash_mob_rave.jpg/330px-UNC_library_flash_mob_rave.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/UNC_library_flash_mob_rave.jpg/440px-UNC_library_flash_mob_rave.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UNC_library_flash_mob_rave.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> At the end of each semester, students organize a 
        <a href="/wiki/Flash_mob" title="Flash mob">flash mob</a> dance party in the library.
        <sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The athletic teams at the university are supported by the Marching Tar Heels, the university's <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching band</a>. The entire 275-member volunteer band is present at every home football game, and smaller <a href="/wiki/Pep_band" title="Pep band">pep bands</a> play at all home basketball games. Each member of the band is also required to play in at least one of five pep bands that play at athletic events of the 26 other sports.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> UNC has a <a href="/wiki/Regional_theatre_in_the_United_States" title="Regional theatre in the United States" class="mw-redirect">regional theater</a> company in residence, the <a href="/wiki/Dramatic_and_performing_arts_at_the_University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill#PlayMakers_Repertory_Company" title="Dramatic and performing arts at the University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">Playmakers Repertory Company</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> and hosts regular dance, drama, and music performances on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> The school has an outdoor stone amphitheatre known as Forest Theatre used for weddings and drama productions.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> Forest Theatre is dedicated to Professor Frederick Koch, the founder of the <a href="/wiki/PlayMakers_Repertory_Company#History_of_the_Carolina_Playmakers" title="PlayMakers Repertory Company">Carolina Playmakers</a> and the father American folk drama.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Many <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities_in_North_America" title="Fraternities and sororities in North America">fraternities and sororities</a> on campus belong to the <a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">National Panhellenic Conference</a> (NPC), Interfraternity Council (IFC), Greek Alliance Council, and <a href="/wiki/National_Pan-Hellenic_Council" title="National Pan-Hellenic Council">National Pan-Hellenic Council</a> (NPHC). As of spring 2010, eighteen percent of undergraduates were Greek (1146 men and 1693 women out of 17,160 total).<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> The total number of community service hours completed for the 2010 spring semester by fraternities and sororities was 51,819 hours (average of 31 hours/person). UNC also offers professional and service fraternities that do not have houses but are still recognized by the school. Some of the campus honor societies include: the Order of the Golden Fleece, the Order of the Grail-Valkyries, the Order of the Old Well, the Order of the Bell Tower, and the Frank Porter Graham Honor Society.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Student government at Carolina is composed of an executive branch headed by the student body president, a legislative branch composed of a student-elected student congress, and a judicial branch which includes the honor court and student supreme court.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> The Judicial Reform Committee created the Instrument of Student Judicial Governance, which outlined the current Honor Code and its means for enforcement in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Daily_Tar_Heel_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Daily_Tar_Heel-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> Currently, Carolina boasts one of the only student-run judicial systems in the nation. All academic and most conduct violations are handled by the student-run Honor System. Prior to that time, the <a href="/wiki/Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies" title="Dialectic and Philanthropic Societies">Dialectic and Philanthropic Societies</a> along with other campus organizations supported student concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dining">Dining</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Dining">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Lenoir Dining Hall was completed in 1939 and opened for service to students when they returned from Christmas holidays in January 1940. The building was named for <a href="/wiki/William_Lenoir_(general)" title="William Lenoir (general)">General William Lenoir</a>, first chairman of the Board of Trustees of the university in 1790. The new Rams Head Dining Hall seats 1,300 people and has a capacity for serving 10,000 meals per day. It has one large dining area, two medium size dining areas, food service staff offices, kitchen, food preparation areas, storage and a Starbucks coffee shop.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Rams Head Dining Center was opened to the students in March 2005. It includes the Rams Head Dining Hall, Starbucks, and the Rams Head Market. It was opened to offer more food service options to the students living on south campus. In addition the dining hall's hours were extended to include the 9&nbsp;pm&nbsp;? 12&nbsp;am period, a time referred to as &quot;Late Night&quot; by students.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Old_East.jpg" class="image"><img alt=" beige, brick building with many windows on the right side of the building." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Old_East.jpg/220px-Old_East.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Old_East.jpg/330px-Old_East.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Old_East.jpg/440px-Old_East.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Old_East.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Old_East" title="Old East">Old East Residence Hall</a>, built in 1793
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>On campus, the Department of Housing and Residential Education manages thirty-two residence halls, grouped into thirteen communities. These communities range from Olde Campus Upper Quad Community which includes <a href="/wiki/Old_East" title="Old East">Old East Residence Hall</a>, the oldest building of the university, to modern communities such as Manning West, completed in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to residence halls, the university oversees an additional eight apartment complexes organized into three communities, Ram Village, Odum Village, and Baity Hill Student Family Housing. Along with themed housing focusing on foreign languages and substance-free living, there are also &quot;living-learning communities&quot; which have been formed for specific social, gender-related, or academic needs.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> An example is UNITAS, sponsored by the Department of Anthropology, where residents are assigned roommates on the basis of cultural or racial differences rather than similarities.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> Three apartment complexes offer housing for families, graduate students, and some upperclassmen.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> Along with the rest of campus, all residence halls, apartments, and their surrounding grounds are <a href="/wiki/Smoking_ban" title="Smoking ban">smoke-free</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2008, 46% of all undergraduates live in university-provided housing.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill_alumni" title="List of University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill alumni">List of University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill alumni</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:James_Knox_Polk_by_GPA_Healy,_1858.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A portrait of a man wearing black while clasping his hands." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/James_Knox_Polk_by_GPA_Healy%2C_1858.jpg/220px-James_Knox_Polk_by_GPA_Healy%2C_1858.jpg" width="220" height="290" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/James_Knox_Polk_by_GPA_Healy%2C_1858.jpg/330px-James_Knox_Polk_by_GPA_Healy%2C_1858.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/James_Knox_Polk_by_GPA_Healy%2C_1858.jpg/440px-James_Knox_Polk_by_GPA_Healy%2C_1858.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:James_Knox_Polk_by_GPA_Healy,_1858.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/James_K._Polk" title="James K. Polk">James K. Polk</a> was President of the United States from 1845 to 1849.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>With over 270,000 living former students,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> North Carolina has one of the largest and most active <a href="/wiki/The_Association_of_Former_Students" title="The Association of Former Students">alumni groups</a> in America. Many Tar Heels have attained local, national, and international prominence. <a href="/wiki/James_K._Polk" title="James K. Polk">James K. Polk</a> served as President of the United States for a single term,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_R._King" title="William R. King">William R. King</a> was the thirteenth Vice President of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> North Carolina has produced many <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senators</a> including <a href="/wiki/Paul_Wellstone" title="Paul Wellstone">Paul Wellstone</a><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lanier_Clingman" title="Thomas Lanier Clingman">Thomas Lanier Clingman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> along with multiple <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House Representatives</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Foxx" title="Virginia Foxx">Virginia Foxx</a><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ike_Franklin_Andrews" title="Ike Franklin Andrews">Ike Franklin Andrews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Algenon_L._Marbley" title="Algenon L. Marbley">Algenon L. Marbley</a><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Settle_(judge)" title="Thomas Settle (judge)">Thomas Settle</a><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> have received positions of federal judgeship. Former <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_War" title="Secretary of War" class="mw-redirect">Secretary of War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_the_Army" title="Secretary of the Army" class="mw-redirect">Secretary of the Army</a> <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Claiborne_Royall" title="Kenneth Claiborne Royall">Kenneth Claiborne Royall</a><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> and the fifth <a href="/wiki/White_House_Press_Secretary" title="White House Press Secretary">White House Press Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_W._Daniels" title="Jonathan W. Daniels">Jonathan W. Daniels</a> were graduates of North Carolina.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Tar Heels have also made a mark on <a href="/wiki/Pop_culture" title="Pop culture" class="mw-redirect">pop culture</a>. <a href="/wiki/Andy_Griffith" title="Andy Griffith">Andy Griffith</a><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/John_Forsythe" title="John Forsythe">John Forsythe</a><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> have become successful actors. <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Scott" title="Stuart Scott">Stuart Scott</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Woody_Durham" title="Woody Durham">Woody Durham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mick_Mixon" title="Mick Mixon">Mick Mixon</a><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> have become sportscasters. Civil War historian and writer <a href="/wiki/Shelby_Foote" title="Shelby Foote">Shelby Foote</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> sportswriter <a href="/wiki/Peter_Gammons" title="Peter Gammons">Peter Gammons</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Lenoir_Chambers" title="Lenoir Chambers">Lenoir Chambers</a><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> all graduated from North Carolina. Other notable writers who have attended UNC include <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wolfe" title="Thomas Wolfe">Thomas Wolfe</a>, who has a memorial on campus; <a href="/wiki/National_Book_Award" title="National Book Award">National Book Award</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Walker_Percy" title="Walker Percy">Walker Percy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hayden_Carruth" title="Hayden Carruth">Hayden Carruth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Frazier" title="Charles Frazier">Charles Frazier</a>; <a href="/wiki/Dos_Passos_Prize" title="Dos Passos Prize">Dos Passos Prize</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Russell_Banks" title="Russell Banks">Russell Banks</a>; <a href="/wiki/National_Book_Critics_Circle_Award" title="National Book Critics Circle Award">National Book Critics Circle Award</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Ben_Fountain" title="Ben Fountain">Ben Fountain</a>; <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> finalist <a href="/wiki/Lydia_Millet" title="Lydia Millet">Lydia Millet</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">New Yorker</a></i> columnist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Mitchell_(writer)" title="Joseph Mitchell (writer)">Joseph Mitchell</a>; <a href="/wiki/Armistead_Maupin" title="Armistead Maupin">Armistead Maupin</a>; and the notable poets <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Ferlinghetti" title="Lawrence Ferlinghetti">Lawrence Ferlinghetti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bollingen_Prize" title="Bollingen Prize">Bollingen Prize</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Bowers" title="Edgar Bowers">Edgar Bowers</a>. <a href="/wiki/Caleb_Bradham" title="Caleb Bradham">Caleb Bradham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> the inventor of the popular <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drink</a> <a href="/wiki/Pepsi-Cola" title="Pepsi-Cola" class="mw-redirect">Pepsi-Cola</a>, was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Dialectic_and_Philanthropic_Societies" title="Dialectic and Philanthropic Societies">Philanthropic Society</a> and the class of 1890.</p> 
     <p>Tar Heels have made their mark on the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_court" title="Basketball court">basketball court</a> with <a href="/wiki/SMU_Mustangs_men%27s_basketball" title="SMU Mustangs men's basketball">Southern Methodist University</a> head coach <a href="/wiki/Larry_Brown_(basketball)" title="Larry Brown (basketball)">Larry Brown</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> title winning coach <a href="/wiki/Roy_Williams_(coach)" title="Roy Williams (coach)">Roy Williams</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers" title="Los Angeles Lakers">Los Angeles Lakers</a> <a href="/wiki/General_manager" title="General manager">general manager</a> <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Kupchak" title="Mitch Kupchak">Mitch Kupchak</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._men%27s_college_basketball_national_player_of_the_year_awards" title="List of U.S. men's college basketball national player of the year awards">college player of the year award</a> winners <a href="/wiki/George_Glamack" title="George Glamack">George Glamack</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Glamack_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glamack-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lennie_Rosenbluth" title="Lennie Rosenbluth">Lennie Rosenbluth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antawn_Jamison" title="Antawn Jamison">Antawn Jamison</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Hansbrough" title="Tyler Hansbrough">Tyler Hansbrough</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame">Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame</a> inductees <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jordan" title="Michael Jordan">Michael Jordan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Billy_Cunningham" title="Billy Cunningham">Billy Cunningham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bob_McAdoo" title="Bob McAdoo">Robert McAdoo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> great defender <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Jones_(basketball,_born_1951)" title="Bobby Jones (basketball, born 1951)">Bobby Jones</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/NBA_All-Star_Game" title="NBA All-Star Game">NBA All-Star</a> <a href="/wiki/Vince_Carter" title="Vince Carter">Vince Carter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> Other notable Tar Heels include football players <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Taylor" title="Lawrence Taylor">Lawrence Taylor</a><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Dr%C3%A9_Bly" title="Dr&eacute; Bly">Dr&eacute; Bly</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> soccer stars <a href="/wiki/Mia_Hamm" title="Mia Hamm">Mia Hamm</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ashlyn_Harris" title="Ashlyn Harris">Ashlyn Harris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heather_O%27Reilly" title="Heather O'Reilly">Heather O'Reilly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meghan_Klingenberg" title="Meghan Klingenberg">Meghan Klingenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Engen" title="Whitney Engen">Whitney Engen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allie_Long" title="Allie Long">Allie Long</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tobin_Heath" title="Tobin Heath">Tobin Heath</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> baseball standouts <a href="/wiki/Dustin_Ackley" title="Dustin Ackley">Dustin Ackley</a><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/B.J._Surhoff" title="B.J. Surhoff" class="mw-redirect">B.J. Surhoff</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> and Olympians <a href="/wiki/April_Heinrichs" title="April Heinrichs">April Heinrichs</a><sup id="cite_ref-ussoccer2000_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ussoccer2000-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vikas_Gowda" title="Vikas Gowda">Vikas Gowda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ussoccer2000_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ussoccer2000-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Many Tar Heels have become business leaders. The leaders include <a href="/wiki/Jason_Kilar" title="Jason Kilar">Jason Kilar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> former CEO of <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a>; <a href="/wiki/Howard_R._Levine" title="Howard R. Levine">Howard R. Levine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> chairman of the board and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Family_Dollar" title="Family Dollar">Family Dollar</a>; <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kolton" title="Paul Kolton">Paul Kolton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> chairman of the <a href="/wiki/American_Stock_Exchange" title="American Stock Exchange">American Stock Exchange</a>; <a href="/wiki/Julian_Robertson" title="Julian Robertson">Julian Robertson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> founder of <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Management_Corp." title="Tiger Management Corp." class="mw-redirect">Tiger Management Corp.</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bill_Ruger" title="Bill Ruger" class="mw-redirect">Bill Ruger</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> founder of <a href="/wiki/Sturm,_Ruger" title="Sturm, Ruger" class="mw-redirect">Sturm, Ruger</a>; <a href="/wiki/Warren_Grice_Elliott" title="Warren Grice Elliott">Warren Grice Elliott</a>, former president of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Line_Railroad" title="Atlantic Coast Line Railroad">Atlantic Coast Line Railroad</a>; <a href="/wiki/Allen_B._Morgan,_Jr." title="Allen B. Morgan, Jr.">Allen B.
